  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11848292929345578275">Sara Crewe, an exceptionally intelligent and imaginative student at Miss Minchin's Select Seminary for Young Ladies, is devastated when her adored, indulgent father dies. Now penniless and banished to a room in the attic, Sara is demeaned, abused, and forced to work as a servant. How this resourceful girl's fortunes change again is at the center of <b>A Little Princess</b>, one o</span>
  <span id="freeText11848292929345578275" style="display:none">Sara Crewe, an exceptionally intelligent and imaginative student at Miss Minchin's Select Seminary for Young Ladies, is devastated when her adored, indulgent father dies. Now penniless and banished to a room in the attic, Sara is demeaned, abused, and forced to work as a servant. How this resourceful girl's fortunes change again is at the center of <b>A Little Princess</b>, one of the best-loved stories in all of children's literature.<br /><br /> This unique and fully annotated edition appends excerpts from <b>Frances Hodgson Burnett</b>'s original 1888 novella <b>Sara Crewe</b> and the stage play that preceded the novel, as well as an early story, "Behind the White Brick," allowing readers to see how A Little Princess evolved. In his delightful introduction, U. C. Knoepflmacher considers the fairy-tale allusions and literary touchstones that place the book among the major works of Victorian literature, and shows it to be an exceptionally rich and resonant novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11848292929345578275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">At four years old, Lottie is the youngest girl in Miss Minchin's seminary. Like the protagonist, Sara, Lottie has no mother. A spoiled child, she's gi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">At four years old, Lottie is the youngest girl in Miss Minchin's seminary. Like the protagonist, Sara, Lottie has no mother. A spoiled child, she's given to tantrums. Sara was the only person able to soothe her in the middle of one of Lottie's screaming fits, and since then became an adopted sort of mother to Lottie, who ever afterward followed her around.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer7289768804651563006">My mother thought it completely foolish of me to buy a hardcover book and then finish it in one night (these were the days before Harry Potter and, besides, we had enough books in our house, in her opinion). But I loved owning this edition with its gorgeous images and, when I gave it to my younger cousins in Singapore, believing myself ready to part with my childhood attachment to a book I wouldn't ever forget, I did mourn its loss, though I was a teenager by then and studying the dead white mal</span>
  <span id="freeText7289768804651563006" style="display:none">My mother thought it completely foolish of me to buy a hardcover book and then finish it in one night (these were the days before Harry Potter and, besides, we had enough books in our house, in her opinion). But I loved owning this edition with its gorgeous images and, when I gave it to my younger cousins in Singapore, believing myself ready to part with my childhood attachment to a book I wouldn't ever forget, I did mourn its loss, though I was a teenager by then and studying the dead white male canon. I'm an awful person, I know, but when I visited my family in Singapore the year before I graduated from college, I noticed the book on their shelf and asked to see it, and my aunt, noticing how my face lit up, asked if I wanted it back.<br /><br />"Really? You mean it? Is that OK?"<br />"Of course, why wouldn't it be?"<br />"Are you sure? Oh, but I'm awful. I guess I didn't know how much it meant to me. You're so wonderful. What can I give you?" <br /><br />I forget what I gave them in exchange, but it certainly held no value compared to this book. Not to be too psychoanalytical, but I suppose my reclaiming the book was a silent protest against my mother (and my unconsciously wanting to reconnect with my father, from whom I'd inherited my love of books). I haven't changed much in all these years. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer868828293" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4103829043502589109"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411964042ra/11305779.gif' width='450' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The movie based on this classic was the first one ever gifted to me and that when I was eight years old. I've always had a thing for princess stories. They’re usually so beautiful and this is no exception.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411964042ra/11305780.gif' width='500' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Although, Sara is not really a princess. But, seeing the way she acts with others, you may possibly think she is. She is kind, generous, and very mature for her age. When I first saw the movie, I was shocked. It was beautiful yet so sad and poignant and the little eight-year-old girl that I was</span>
  <span id="freeText4103829043502589109" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411964042ra/11305779.gif" width="450" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The movie based on this classic was the first one ever gifted to me and that when I was eight years old. I've always had a thing for princess stories. They’re usually so beautiful and this is no exception.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411964042ra/11305780.gif" width="500" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Although, Sara is not really a princess. But, seeing the way she acts with others, you may possibly think she is. She is kind, generous, and very mature for her age. When I first saw the movie, I was shocked. It was beautiful yet so sad and poignant and the little eight-year-old girl that I was did not understand everything. To be honest, the ending of the movie is quite abrupt and not very well-explained while in the book it is.<br><br>That said, reading the book was way better than watching the movie, as it usually is with classics and books in general. Everything is clear and explained and you get to see, even more, how Sara is one admirable girl and that she is someone people don’t forget after crossing her path. The things she does are impressive and the fact that she thinks about others before herself even more. She’s the kind of person I wish to become one day.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411964042ra/11305781.gif" width="500" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Every sort of character is included in this story from the kindest to the coldest one. Miss Minchin was quite something. I rarely see such a woman that can be so cruel and cold-heartened. It’s very hard to like her but that doesn’t mean that her character was a weakness to the story since we need villains. The world and people living in it aren’t perfect and she, and some others, are the proof of it.<br><br>The story was wonderful and sad but it wasn’t what you may call a masterpiece. It was a good one, even though the plot has some repetitiveness. That’s why I can’t bring myself to give it a five star rating. Have I read this book when I was younger, I probably would have loved it even more but the seventeen-year-old that I am has read many other classics and must admit that this wasn’t comparable to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1885.Pride_and_Prejudice" title="Pride and Prejudice by Jane Austen" rel="nofollow noopener">Pride and Prejudice</a>’s or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/890.Of_Mice_and_Men" title="Of Mice and Men by John Steinbeck" rel="nofollow noopener">Of Mice and Men</a>’s plot quality for example (even though I know those are very different stories.) Although, the reason why I still liked this so much is because of all the beautiful themes that are included in the story. They can be heart-warming and at the same time heart-breaking but definitely <i>definitely</i> beautiful.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411964042ra/11305782.gif" width="500" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The writing was very good and the atmosphere powerful. I’ve also read, by this author, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2998.The_Secret_Garden" title="The Secret Garden by Frances Hodgson Burnett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret Garden</a> which I enjoyed although not as much as this one. Still, I can tell that this author had such a talent in creating and writing stories. I wish she was still alive for someone that has written such a story sure must be a kind and intelligent person. <br><br>By the way, a reason why I don’t hurry to read every classic existing is because I want to still have some to read when I’ll be sixty years old for they are, each one of them, precious and there aren’t that many of them, sadly.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3008.A_Little_Princess" title="A Little Princess by Frances Hodgson Burnett" rel="nofollow noopener">A Little Princess</a> deserves, in my opinion, to be read by every person in this world, boy or girl, man or woman. It is for everyone. If you’re looking for another classic with similar themes, you might want to check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1934.Little_Women__Little_Women___1_" title="Little Women (Little Women, #1) by Louisa May Alcott" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Women</a> as well, which was <i>wonderful wonderful wonderful</i>.<br></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_977172813" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/977172813" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480492067p2/32532774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/977172813?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=children">children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer977172813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15959886773696998503">"Whatever comes," she said, "cannot alter one thing. If I am a princess in rags and tatters, I can be a princess inside. It would be easy to be a princess if I were dressed in cloth of gold, but it is a great deal more of a triumph to be one all the time when no one knows it." <br/><br/>Much can be said about the improbabilities in the plot, about the desperate sentimentality and caricature of Victorian England's boarding school system. It doesn't matter. <br/><br/>To me, Sarah Crewe will always remain a symbol for</span>
  <span id="freeText15959886773696998503" style="display:none">"Whatever comes," she said, "cannot alter one thing. If I am a princess in rags and tatters, I can be a princess inside. It would be easy to be a princess if I were dressed in cloth of gold, but it is a great deal more of a triumph to be one all the time when no one knows it." <br /><br />Much can be said about the improbabilities in the plot, about the desperate sentimentality and caricature of Victorian England's boarding school system. It doesn't matter. <br /><br />To me, Sarah Crewe will always remain a symbol for inner strength, perseverance and values winning over greed, sadism and abusive power. I can't recall how many times I read my hardcover copy as a young girl, shivering with anger and fear when the young heiress thinks she has lost everything and is turned into an unpaid maid at the school where she used to be a shining star. <br /><br />Quite often, I think of her when I enter a bakery on a cold day, the smell of fresh bread making me instantly hungry. I think of the hungry girl, and how much she must have craved the buns she bought for a coin she found. And I know it is a simple show-effect on the part of Frances Hodgson Burnett to make Sarah hand over the buns to a starving girl sitting outside the bakery. It is not realistic! We are human beings. We a greedy, egotistical, trained and constructed to guarantee our own selfish survival first of all. We don't give away our bread. We hoard it until it gets moldy and can't be eaten by anyone!<br /><br />And yet - Sarah Crewe, the fictional perfect human being, clever, kind, using her power to help, rather than to destroy others, makes my heart feel a tiny bit better each time I think of her. She is not realistic, and nor is the poetical justice in the novel, giving back the wealth she had thought she lost as some kind of divine reward for being a good sport when she lost it.<br /><br />Does it really matter whether this story is exaggerated? If I can choose to give my children one of the countless bestselling young adult novels that show humanity in its worst egomania, or this tale of friendship, genuine care and power of imagination, I won't have to think twice. I like to imagine that people loving Sarah Crewe might start seeing those around themselves that are "hungrier than she was herself", and that they might feel that they can offer a bun or two from their bakery basket as a result of their reading. If reading inspires, I like to think this one inspires more than a dire account of teenage violence and crime...<br /><br />Try being a princess no matter what - that's what I believe in, loving my fairy tales still!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15959886773696998503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15846751618774487292">A Little Princess, Frances Hodgson Burnett <br/><br/>A Little Princess is a children's novel by Frances Hodgson Burnett, first published as a book in 1905. <br/><br/>Captain Crewe, a wealthy English widower, has been raising his only child, Sara, in India where he is stationed with the British Army. Because the Indian climate is considered too harsh for children, British families living there traditionally send their children to boarding school back home in England. <br/><br/>The captain enrolls his young daughter at Miss Mi</span>
  <span id="freeText15846751618774487292" style="display:none">A Little Princess, Frances Hodgson Burnett <br /><br />A Little Princess is a children's novel by Frances Hodgson Burnett, first published as a book in 1905. <br /><br />Captain Crewe, a wealthy English widower, has been raising his only child, Sara, in India where he is stationed with the British Army. Because the Indian climate is considered too harsh for children, British families living there traditionally send their children to boarding school back home in England. <br /><br />The captain enrolls his young daughter at Miss Minchin's boarding school for girls in London, and dotes on his daughter so much that he orders and pays the headmistress for special treatment and exceptional luxuries for Sara, such as a private room for her with a personal maid and a separate sitting room, along with Sara's own private carriage and a pony. Miss Minchin openly fawns over Sara for her money, but secretly and jealously despises her for her wealth. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز هفتم ماه آگوست سال 2006 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: سارا کوچولو: یا ماجراهای خانه خانم مین چین؛ نویسنده: فرانسس هاجسون (هاجسن) بارنت (برنت)؛ مترجم علی کاتبی؛ تهران، نشر اشاره؛ چاپ سوم 1370؛ در 82 ص؛ چاپ چهارم 1372؛ چاپ پنجم 1375؛ موضوع: داستانهای کودکان از نویسندگان بریتانیایی - سده 20م<br /><br />عنوان: سارا کوچولو؛ نویسنده: فرانسس هاجسون (هاجسن) بارنت (برنت)؛ مترجم: هادی عادلپور؛ تهران، کوشش، 1375، در 192ص؛ <br /><br />عنوان: سارا کروو؛ نویسنده: فرانسس هاجسون (هاجسن) بارنت (برنت)؛ مترجم: مهدی فیاض؛ مشهد، نشر موحد؛ 1376؛ در 96ص؛<br /><br />عنوان: ساراکرو؛ نویسنده: فرانسس هاچسون برنت؛ مترجم: مترجم: حسن قائم مقامی؛ تهران، شهر کتاب، هرمس؛ 1382؛ در 320ص؛ شابک 9643632121؛ <br /><br />عنوان: س‍ارا ک‍وچ‍ول‍و؛ ن‍وش‍ت‍ه‌: ف‍ران‍س‍ی‍س‌ ه‍اج‍س‍ن‌ ب‍رن‍ت‌؛ مت‍رج‍م: ه‍روس‌ ش‍ب‍ان‍ی‌؛ وی‍راس‍ت‍ار: اح‍م‍د س‍ل‍طان‍ی‌.؛ تهران، بلوط، 1376؛ در 152ص؛ شابک 9649096612؛<br /><br />عنوان: س‍ارا ک‍ورو: ش‍اه‍زاده‌ خ‍ان‍م‌ ک‍وچ‍ک‌؛ نویسنده: ف‍ران‍س‌ه‍اج‍س‍ن‌ ب‍رن‍ت‌؛ مت‍رج‍م: رام‍ک‌ ن‍ی‍ک‌طل‍ب‌؛ ت‍ه‍ران‌ ق‍دی‍ان‍ی‌، ک‍ت‍اب‍ه‍ای‌ ب‍ن‍ف‍ش‍ه‌‏‫، 1383؛ در 246ص؛ شابک: 9789644175909؛ ‬ چاپ پنجم 1390؛ چاپ هفتم 1391؛ چاپ دهم 1397؛<br /><br />پرنسس کوچک یک رمان کودکانه اثر «فرانسس هاجسون برنت» است، که نخستین بار به شکل کتاب در سال 1905میلادی چاپ شد. این رمان نسخه‌ ای گسترش یافته از داستان کوتاه «سارا کرو: یا، آنچه در مدرسه خانم مینچین اتفاق افتاد» است<br /><br /> ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_1766762037" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1766762037" />
    <a title="WhatIReallyRead" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52500467-whatireallyread"><img alt="WhatIReallyRead" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483674713p2/52500467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1766762037?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="WhatIReallyRead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="WhatIReallyRead" href="/user/show/52500467-whatireallyread">WhatIReallyRead</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141321127" href="/book/show/2302797.A_Little_Princess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=hated">hated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=physical-book">physical-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1766762037" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14174207714382805232"><b>UNPOPULAR OPINION TIME. Sorry folks.</b><br/><br/>Meet the characters:<br/><br/><b>Sara aka the Little Princess</b> is described as (and I'm only using words written explicitly in the book): thin, pale, with striking green eyes too big for her face (now I know where so many YA heroine's descriptions come from LOL), clever, good, serious, quick at her lessons, proud, brave, generous, hospitable, unconquerable, amiable, good-tempered, having good manners. She speaks fluent French, though she'd never learned it. She also speaks </span>
  <span id="freeText14174207714382805232" style="display:none"><b>UNPOPULAR OPINION TIME. Sorry folks.</b><br><br>Meet the characters:<br><br><b>Sara aka the Little Princess</b> is described as (and I'm only using words written explicitly in the book): thin, pale, with striking green eyes too big for her face (now I know where so many YA heroine's descriptions come from LOL), clever, good, serious, quick at her lessons, proud, brave, generous, hospitable, unconquerable, amiable, good-tempered, having good manners. She speaks fluent French, though she'd never learned it. She also speaks fluent Hindi. <br><br><b>Sara's father</b> is described as young, beautiful, nice and clever.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1563638114i/27860748._SY540_.jpg" alt="A Little Princess by Frances Hodgson Burnett - Puffin Classics" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Ermengarde (aka Sara's best friend)</b> is explicitly described as fat, stupid, not clever, having a slow little mind, vulgar, forgetful and forgettable. <br><br><b>Lottie</b> is another one of Sara's friends, a young child. She's also fat and stupid, but also ill-tempered and capricious, prone to throwing tantrums.<br><br><b>Beckie, aka the servant</b>, is another Sara's friend. She's always described as poor-poor-poor Becky. Also stupid.<br><br><b>Lavinia, aka the nemesis</b>, is described as horrid, nasty, priggish, sneering, and jealous.<br><br><b>Miss Minchin, aka the headmistress</b>, is described as rude, acid, harsh, domineering, hard-hearted, mean, vulgar. Also, she doesn't know French and doesn't try to learn it, being the headmistress of a top school for young ladies in XIX England. Hmmm...<br><br><b>Cook</b> is described as vulgar and insolent.<br><br><b>Beggar girl</b> seen on the street: with a stupid look of suffering, frightful, little ravening savage, poor little wild animal.<br><br>Do you see a pattern here? I do.<br><br>1) Sara is a total Mary Sue, so is her kin (dad). They are oh-so-clever (even though Father never set aside any of his money for his daughter in case something happened, didn't even pay her school forward for even a day. Is that very clever?)<br><br>2) Sara's friends are all fat and stupid, and their only redeeming quality is that they worship her and trail her like puppies with unwavering loyalty and admiration. <br><br>3) Sara's enemies are all dumb and rude.<br><br>Do I have to say I didn't adore a book with such characters? <br><br><b>WHAT ABOUT THE PLOT?</b><br><br>So. Sara is awesome and rich. She briefly becomes poor but stays awesome. Her friends continue to worship her; her enemies expose their shallow, awful true natures. Then Sara becomes rich again, remaining awesome as ever, and punishing all who were mean to her. <b>Yup, Sara never changes in her awesomeness, she doesn't need a character arc. Instead, the whole world around her makes an arc. Brilliant.</b><br><br>Don't even get me started that a child who has always been given all she wants, has never heard the word "no" and had -literally- servants and slaves at her beck and call - isn't spoiled, but is instead wise and teaches her wisdom to the adults around her. Sure, because wisdom isn't something you learn through error and hardship. You're just born with it if you're a true Princess inside. <br><br><b>WHAT MADE ME WANT TO GOUGE MY EYES OUT</b><br><br>Was the complete and unwavering snobbism of Sara and the author. <br><br><i>"It's not your fault that you are stupid"</i> - says Sara to her BFF Ermengarde. How nice and kind, right? <br><br><i>I tried not to be a princess. I tried!</i> - but failed. Who could blame you, Sara? <br><br><i>I can give buns and bread to the populace!</i> - says Sara exuberantly, when she becomes rich again.<br><br><i>"You couldn't look like a street beggar, you haven't a street beggar face," "...clothes to make her look somehow like a servant"</i> - um, so what is a "beggar face" and what do servants look like? Not like humans, just in different clothes? <br><br>Everyone keeps beating themselves up about how much Sara is working (at the time she is poor), but no one pays any mind to Becky, who is of comparable age and actually works more and also harder. Sara deserves all the sympathy because she used to be rich, you see! The whole London filled with hungry children working way too hard is of no concern because they look like servants and have beggar faces. <br><br>Miss Minchin is portrayed as a monster because she made Sara work when she turned from crazy rich to a beggar. Sara is, in fact, indebted to Minchin, because not only did her father not pay forward, he also didn't cover some hefty bills. Minchin does a good thing not throwing Sara out and also adapting her to a change of station. Because her station is indeed very much changed. What should she have done? Ignored reality, to make Sara face it later, even more harshly? Sure, Minchin could have been softer to a child who's just lost her father. But of course, the author wouldn't have that. <br><br><b>So I absolutely HATED every page of this book.</b> As I hated Little Women and Black Beauty, as a matter of fact. Maybe catching up on children's classics I haven't read is a bad idea.<br><br><b>P.S. (20.07.2019)</b> In fairness, I've just finished a different book by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2041.Frances_Hodgson_Burnett" title="Frances Hodgson Burnett" rel="nofollow noopener">Frances Hodgson Burnett</a> - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2998.The_Secret_Garden" title="The Secret Garden by Frances Hodgson Burnett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret Garden</a> - which is a children's classic as well. And I loved it and gave it 5 stars. So it seems too early to give up on the genre or even the author. The Little Princess was just not for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14174207714382805232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2176094261" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2176094261" />
    <a title="Piya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22914826-piya"><img alt="Piya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536570213p2/22914826.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2176094261?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Piya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Piya" href="/user/show/22914826-piya">Piya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2176094261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12150339717115361793"><br/><i>
  <b>“If I am a princess in rags and tatters, I can be a princess inside. It would be easy to be a princess if I were dressed in cloth of gold, but it is a great deal more of a triumph to be one all the time when no one knows it.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>What an adorable, heartwarming little book !! I believe this is the second classic that I have read ever( yeah, not a huge fan of classics :-|).The plot is a very simple one .But, as an old wise man once stated “Mysteries and complexities have their own charm but sometim</span>
  <span id="freeText12150339717115361793" style="display:none"><br><i>
  <b>“If I am a princess in rags and tatters, I can be a princess inside. It would be easy to be a princess if I were dressed in cloth of gold, but it is a great deal more of a triumph to be one all the time when no one knows it.”</b>
</i><br><br>What an adorable, heartwarming little book !! I believe this is the second classic that I have read ever( yeah, not a huge fan of classics :-|).The plot is a very simple one .But, as an old wise man once stated “Mysteries and complexities have their own charm but sometimes the simplest stories are the nicest”. Best way to sum it up!<br><br>It is the story of a little girl named Sara. She is remarkable…an intelligent, kind girl…a bit strange at times…but overall remarkable. She is super rich and her father spares no expenses to fulfill any of her wishes. But she doesn’t let it go to her head. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411964042ra/11305780.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Will she be the same person if the circumstances were to change?? What determines what kind of a person you are? Well, no suspense here …we find out soon enough . Something really horrible happens …and she turns from princess to a servant overnight. What stands out though, is her unique way of dealing with these extraordinarily horrible circumstances .She uses make-beliefs to draw strength and cooks up stories to stay positive.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1516333080ra/24891650.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, every story needs a villain. And Oh yes …we get the cruelest of them all- Ms. Minchin. I hated her with all my heart!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1516332974ra/24891649.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, a wonderful story with a beautiful theme/ message. But I felt there were some repetitiveness and the plot was too simple. If I had been younger , probably it would have been a 5-star read . But, still it’s a great book for everyone. And if you are in need for a little pick-me-up …it’s the perfect one ! ;) <br><i>
  <b>“There’s nothing so strong as rage, except what makes you hold it in – that’s stronger.”</b>
</i><br><br>Thank u <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/36464272-avinash" rel="nofollow noopener"> Mr. Grumpy</a> for the awesome rec and BR ! :) <br><br></span>

  <span id="freeText910850497231055516" style="display:none">I managed to write an almost-full review of this book. I liked the first half better than the second, probably because, again, the movie version of the story is just a lot more entertaining. <br /><br />There are also a lot more villains in the book. It's more like Sara in a sea of people who are average-to-bad, which is kind of a weird message for a children's book.<br /><br />Anyway. I'm glad I finally read this, though. It was good, and if I'd read the book first I wouldn't be judging it so harshly.<br /><br />Bottom line: Yeah, give it a try. Look at that goddamn cover!</span>

<div id="review_1263870468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1263870468" />
    <a title="Calista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16731747-calista"><img alt="Calista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436384393p2/16731747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1263870468?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Calista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Calista" href="/user/show/16731747-calista">Calista</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">magical realism</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=bage-middle-grade">bage-middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=z-frances-hodgson-burnett">z-frances-hodgson-burnett</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=1900-1929">1900-1929</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-drama-tragedy">genre-drama-tragedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1263870468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer744956595838784986">One of my favorite books of all time.<br/><br/>Okay, this needs an update. I love magical realism and as far as I can tell, this is one of the first books that I read about magical realism. This book moved me so much. The world seems to crumble around the 'little princess', but she keeps her hope that things are better with story and imagination, no matter the real world. She uplifts those girls around her. <br/><br/>She is left at a boarding school for girls while her father goes to be in a war. He sets her up wit</span>
  <span id="freeText744956595838784986" style="display:none">One of my favorite books of all time.<br /><br />Okay, this needs an update. I love magical realism and as far as I can tell, this is one of the first books that I read about magical realism. This book moved me so much. The world seems to crumble around the 'little princess', but she keeps her hope that things are better with story and imagination, no matter the real world. She uplifts those girls around her. <br /><br />She is left at a boarding school for girls while her father goes to be in a war. He sets her up with the best room and things and he does his best to spoil her from afar. She is kind to the girls around her and spins fabulous tales that change the lives of the girls around her. It gives them strength and hope and a sense of belonging, of home. <br /><br />Then, her father goes missing and the money stops and the head mistress who put up with the girls shenanigans lets her hatred out and the girl has to become a servant in the school. She continues to help the girls around her, she continues to spin tales.<br /><br />Our perspective in life really does define our reality. I love this story because I strive to be this way, but I fall so short. I want to be able to live this so much. When life gets difficult, I tend to give up and shrink away. Then I have to build myself up all over again. I want to be more like Sarah and able to withstand tough times. <br /><br />This would be a desert island book for me. I need that romantic view of life. I'm also a 4 on the enneagram which is the romantic and I just see the world through that romantic lens, so it makes sense stories about romantic ideals will speak to me. This is the best of the best. </span>
  <a data-text-id="744956595838784986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14044038043427461555" style="display:none">This was actually really nice. An uplifting tale, where the heroine wins out and the villain fails (screw you Miss Minchen!) <br />Sara Crewe is a well off young lady, whose father sends her to a boarding school in London so she can be educated. <br />Despite her upbringing being given her every hearts desire, Sara doesn't act like a brat. She shares what she has with the other girls - apart from two awful jealous ones. (There's always a vindictive girl and her sidekick). <br />So when her father dies suddenly having lost their fortune Sara is reduced to a life of servitude and hunger. <br />Despite this she pretends in her heart that she is a princess just going through hard times and that things will improve. <br />It's a wonderful story with an ending that everyone would love. It restores faith in karma and good triumphing over bad. I thoroughly enjoyed it. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1830509937?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780694012367" href="/book/show/1182963.A_Little_Princess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=classics-i-ve-read">classics-i-ve-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=best-books-i-ve-ever-read">best-books-i-ve-ever-read</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830509937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16493381486119068173"><b>Full review now posted!</b><br/><br/>A buddy read with my friend <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/18278210-adpibookworm' rel='nofollow noopener'>Missy</a>!<br/><br/>Some books don’t hold up well over time. Others improve with every reading. This is a book that is firmly in the latter category for me. I liked this book a lot when I was a child. I love it as an adult. Maybe I’ve grown to adore this book because, as I age, the premise of the book and the lessons it teaches strike my heart harder. I’ve never experienced highs quite as high as those Sara Crewe experiences, and I’ve never suffered through l</span>
  <span id="freeText16493381486119068173" style="display:none"><b>Full review now posted!</b><br /><br />A buddy read with my friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/18278210-adpibookworm" rel="nofollow noopener">Missy</a>!<br /><br />Some books don’t hold up well over time. Others improve with every reading. This is a book that is firmly in the latter category for me. I liked this book a lot when I was a child. I love it as an adult. Maybe I’ve grown to adore this book because, as I age, the premise of the book and the lessons it teaches strike my heart harder. I’ve never experienced highs quite as high as those Sara Crewe experiences, and I’ve never suffered through lows quite as low as Sara is forced to endure. But, like everyone, I have experienced triumphs and tragedies. The more I go through in my life, the more I respect little Sara Crewe, a little princess if ever there was one, and how she handled everything both happy or horrific that life threw her way. She always carried herself as the little princess she pretended to be, whether dressed in tattered rags or extravagant riches. She shared what she had with those less fortunate, even when she didn’t really have enough for herself. Sara endured. And if Sara can endure, so can I. My story can be her story in the disguise of my times, hidden within the setting of my life.<br /><br /><blockquote>“Everything’s a story - You are a story - I am a story.”</blockquote><br /><br />I don’t want to say much about the story, though I know it’s a classic and thus the plot is probably already known to anyone who reads this review. If you haven’t read this book, please do. It’s short and it’s lovely and it reminds readers that the way we view ourselves and the actions spawned from that view truly matters. It also reminds us to see others as people, no matter their station in life, and to give freely. Is there any better way to wrap yourself in Christmas spirit than by remembering to give unto others as Christ gave to us? That’s what Sara Crewe’s story does for me. <br /><br /><blockquote>“If nature has made you for a giver, your hands are born open, and so is your heart. And though there may be times when your hands are empty, your heart is always full, and you can give things out of that—warm things, kind things, sweet things—help and comfort and laughter—and sometimes gay, kind laughter is the best help of all.”</blockquote><br /><br />Merry Christmas. May you remember the true reason for the season. And if your memory should fail, let little Sara Crewe remind you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16493381486119068173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2316847207" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2316847207?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catherine" href="/user/show/61672374-catherine">Catherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780147513991" href="/book/show/20893526-a-little-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61672374-catherine?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61672374-catherine?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2316847207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16115404917548713903">My heart is so full after reading this. Years ago, I got the movie A Little Princess for my birthday. I had never heard anything about it before, but little did I know that I would break the DVD player watching it so many times. Like the movie, the book is beautiful. There really is no other word that can accurately describe it. <br/><br/>I've never felt as connected to a protagonist as I did to Sara. This little girl had the biggest, most generous heart and no matter how bad her situation got, her charac</span>
  <span id="freeText16115404917548713903" style="display:none">My heart is so full after reading this. Years ago, I got the movie A Little Princess for my birthday. I had never heard anything about it before, but little did I know that I would break the DVD player watching it so many times. Like the movie, the book is beautiful. There really is no other word that can accurately describe it. <br /><br />I've never felt as connected to a protagonist as I did to Sara. This little girl had the biggest, most generous heart and no matter how bad her situation got, her character remained pure; even when she had nothing to her name she still put others before herself and never wanted pity. When she was grieving the loss of her father and went from being treated like a princess to being treated like a slave, I wanted so badly to save her. It made me want to find a way into the pages to take all her sadness and pain away because she deserved none of it. <br /><br />This is one of those books that you should encourage your kids to read when they are young. Not to say that it isn't a book for adults, because it is, but I think children especially would benefit from reading it as they are most impressionable. As I was reading, I was overcome with a compelling desire to adopt Sara’s open-heartedness—it just made me want to be a better person which I think is a really special reaction to a book. Honestly every time my heart cracked and pieced back together was worth it and I would suffer a million times over if it meant that I had the honor of being touched by this story forever.<br /><br />My favourite quote in the whole book:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“If nature has made you for a giver, your hands are born open, and so is your heart; and though there may be times when your hands are empty, your heart is always full, and you can give things out of that—warm things, kind things, sweet things—help and comfort and laughter—and sometimes gay, kind laughter is the best help of all.”</b>
</i> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16115404917548713903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2477409523" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="~Bookishly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28323108-bookishly"><img alt="~Bookishly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605967142p2/28323108.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2477409523?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Bookishly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Bookishly" href="/user/show/28323108-bookishly">~Bookishly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28323108-bookishly?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28323108-bookishly?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2477409523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4639587267531130411">This was just what I needed. This book was beautifully heart-warming, and I must confess, my heart is most certainly warmed. I remember loving the film of "A little Princess" many years ago, and it has remained a firm favourite with me. Even though the story in the film is slightly different to the original book, I enjoyed both, in a similar way. Actually, I now have a distinct urge to go and watch the film! <br/><br/>"If I am a princess in rags and tatters, I can be a princess inside. It would be easy to</span>
  <span id="freeText4639587267531130411" style="display:none">This was just what I needed. This book was beautifully heart-warming, and I must confess, my heart is most certainly warmed. I remember loving the film of "A little Princess" many years ago, and it has remained a firm favourite with me. Even though the story in the film is slightly different to the original book, I enjoyed both, in a similar way. Actually, I now have a distinct urge to go and watch the film! <br /><br />"If I am a princess in rags and tatters, I can be a princess inside. It would be easy to be a princess if I were dressed in cloth of gold, but it is a great deal more of a triumph to be one all the time when no one knows it.” <br /><br />I enjoyed the first half of the book more, in comparison to the second. Maybe this is because I feel it follows the film more, plus, there are some beautiful and incredible quotes, that really touched me. It also became apparent rather quickly, that there are many more villains in the book, which really, I think is slightly strange for a children's book. But damn, I have to say, I despised Ms Minchin. She really was such a terrible person, and each time she abused Sara, I felt quite angry inside. (Yes, some books have a profound effect on me.) <br /><br />Overall, this is a wonderful story, with a prominent message, and I think I could definitely enjoy this again, at some point in the future.<br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText15966399304395861611" style="display:none">"When one was sitting by a warm fire in a big, glowing room, it was quite delightful to hear how cold it could be in an attic."<br /><br />This might be commonly classified as a children's book, but I absolutely loved it. The story is give your a blast of all kinds of emotions throughout the story, and how the protagonist, Sarah Crewe faces and reacts to each of them in quite a wonderful way. The way how each supporting character complements the story is excellent, and adds much impact.<br /><br />' “You see, I know what it is to be hungry, and it is very hard when one cannot even pretend it away.” '<br /><br />This book will make your laugh, sad, cry, and happy while submersing you in one of the loveliest plots of all time. It's true that certain things seems a bit too perfect, but I guess it's best that way, considering this is indeed a children's book. Also, the lessons are plentiful, specially in the middle part of the story, which will be invaluable to any child. If you have not read this book - regardless what age you are in right now - give it a chance, for, I think, this is something that has no age limit.<br /><br />"She had learned to know how comforting a smile, even from a stranger, may be."</span>
  <a data-text-id="15966399304395861611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12138699255977834820">The movie adaptation of this book was my beloved, childhood favourite, yet, for some reason, I had never read the book. I was pleasantly surprised to find how accurate my favourite film was to the classic text it originated from.<br/><br/>I find it odd how I adored this story so, when my favourite childhood read was Frances Hodgson Burnett's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2998.The_Secret_Garden' title='The Secret Garden by Frances Hodgson Burnett' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Secret Garden</a>.   <span id="freeText12138699255977834820" style="display:none">The movie adaptation of this book was my beloved, childhood favourite, yet, for some reason, I had never read the book. I was pleasantly surprised to find how accurate my favourite film was to the classic text it originated from.<br /><br />I find it odd how I adored this story so, when my favourite childhood read was Frances Hodgson Burnett's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2998.The_Secret_Garden" title="The Secret Garden by Frances Hodgson Burnett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret Garden</a>. I loved the former for the pure-hearted and eternally kind protagonist and adored the latter for the unlikable, cross and bad-tempered one. The two differing protagonists dually delighted me, however dissimilar they appeared, and I believe the author has a powerful gift in creating characters children (and adults, too!) can find all sides of themselves in.<br /><br />Asides from the lovable characters, this book also has a poignant story-line that completely enraptured me. Sara Crewe's riches-to-rags-to-riches story was a charming one, but what completely captivated me was in how she dealt with her fate. She remained eternally optimistic and often used fairy tale and stories created inside her own head as a brief escape from her plight. She was gifted with a pure character and a generous soul and instead of appearing as a two-dimensional 'goody good' character, she instilled in me a yearning to be a better individual and to channel some of her spirit.<br /><br />The parts that brought me to tears, both then and now, was Sara's belief that every female was a princess at heart, and so it is only fitting to end this review with a quote that sums up exactly what is so endearing about this book:<br /><br /><i>"Whatever comes," she said, "cannot alter one thing. If I am a princess in rags and tatters, I can be a princess inside. It would be easy to be a princess if I were dressed in cloth of gold, but it is a great deal more of a triumph to be one all the time when no one knows it.”</i></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9417442496945699072">Downloaded this one in audio form from <b>Librivox</b> as well. <br/><br/>This is one of my all time favourite books. I first read it when I was thirteen years old and a bit of an outcast at my school and it gave me strength to move on. Her way of pretending things was very familiar to me and I got so sucked into the magic of the story.<br/>Hearing it now, I was afraid it would prove childish, as childhood favourites often do. But to my delight it didn't. Sarah was a bit naive at times, which doesn't conflict with th</span>
  <span id="freeText9417442496945699072" style="display:none">Downloaded this one in audio form from <b>Librivox</b> as well. <br /><br />This is one of my all time favourite books. I first read it when I was thirteen years old and a bit of an outcast at my school and it gave me strength to move on. Her way of pretending things was very familiar to me and I got so sucked into the magic of the story.<br />Hearing it now, I was afraid it would prove childish, as childhood favourites often do. But to my delight it didn't. Sarah was a bit naive at times, which doesn't conflict with the fact that she's a little girl, and the story was as charming as I remembered it.<br /> <br />There's a lot of moral and reproach in the book, but the author manages to keep it lighthearted, and to make you yourself wish to become a better person. This book and 'The secret garden' are much better in that way than 'Little Lord Fauntleroy', which is absolutly awful, and which I haven't even been able to finish. Here, the people are not perfect, but each is good in his own way.<br /><br />And of course there's the magic transformation of the attic, which I'll always remember, but which has somehow made less of an impression on me this time than it did last.<br /><br />The only thing which disturbed me was, as another person mentioned here, the hints of orientalism. But you have to remember that that was the way people thought in those times in England. You can compare in to the fact that in the 19th century most of the writers were vaguly antisemetic - you can find it in Dickens, in Verne. So just keep in mind that it was the norm at the time.<br /><br />14.7.07</span>

<div id="review_1883030358" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1883030358" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277905205p2/1166663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1883030358?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781497665675" href="/book/show/25111623-a-little-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166663-carol?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1883030358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17081037593366091435"><b>The Hook</b> - My GR friend Stephanie loved this story as a child. Stephanie owns many editions of her beloved book and her re-reads of this have not disappointed her. Honestly I had never heard of it. I have read <u>A Secret Garden</u> and wondered why <u>A Little Princess</u> never made my childhood reading. I would have loved to have this read out loud to me at that age. Stephanie did suggest an audio version available on Hoopla. I may listen to a bit of this but decided to just take the plunge and found an ed</span>
  <span id="freeText17081037593366091435" style="display:none"><b>The Hook</b> - My GR friend Stephanie loved this story as a child. Stephanie owns many editions of her beloved book and her re-reads of this have not disappointed her. Honestly I had never heard of it. I have read <u>A Secret Garden</u> and wondered why <u>A Little Princess</u> never made my childhood reading. I would have loved to have this read out loud to me at that age. Stephanie did suggest an audio version available on Hoopla. I may listen to a bit of this but decided to just take the plunge and found an edition on my library’s subscription to Freading. <br /><br /><b>The Line(s)</b> - <i>"Sara often thought afterward that the house was somehow exactly like Miss Minchin. It was respectable and well furnished, but everything in it was ugly; and the very armchairs seemed to have hard bones in them.”</i><br /><br /><b>The Sinker</b> - <u>A Little Princess</u> was published in 1905 by author Frances Hodgson Burnett and is suggested for audiences of 10-13 year olds. At this time of my life I was probably just leaving behind series books like Nancy Drew and Cherry Ames, just on the cusp of rolling over to more adult novels. If I had read this rags to riches story a few years earlier I am certain I would have found the imagery delightful and would have been fascinated by Sara’s world, one in which she wears such beautiful clothing so descriptively described in all its finery.<br /><br />Sara Crewe is quite young when the story begins. Her father, Captain Crewe, a wealthy Englishman living in India brings Sara to England for her formal schooling, leaving her in the hands of the owner, Miss Minchin. Sara status and privilege really get under Minchin’s skin and though Minchin is known to be cruel, Sara gets more than her share of her nasty disposition. But Sara remains kind, always trying to look at the bright side of life, making lemonade out of lemons so to speak. Sara’s gift of storytelling, her ability to empathize with the girls who are bullied by their peers and her willingness to do what must be done, endear her to most but not all. How she becomes called Princess is key part of the story. There are marvelous characters throughout these pages, including a doll, with her divine garments and accoutrements, an attic girl named Becky, and even Melchisedec; oh, I’m not telling you who he is.<br /><br />The parting of Sara and her father is very hard to witness. As the time for him to return to India grows closer it’s decided that Sara will be given a new doll, but not just any doll. Her name is to be Emily and she will be Sara’s friend.<br /><br />"I want her to look as if she wasn’t a doll really”, Sara said. “I want her to look as if <i>she listens</i> when I talk to her. The trouble with dolls, papa” –and she put her head on one side and reflected as she said it—“the trouble with dolls is that they never seem to <i>hear</i>.” <br /><br />When Sara’s father diamond mine deal fails and he suddenly dies leaving Sara penniless, her life spirals from wealth to poverty quite quickly. The change in her life and its resolution has the fairytale appeal that makes this story charming.<br /><br />I’m not certain how children of today would enjoy this book. The language is old fashioned and the story doesn’t have the modern zing of today’s movies, TV, games or books. It is simplistic and offers much that is black or white, yet still has themes of goodness and evil to challenge discussion. And yet, given the right child, the right person to share the story with, I could see it being a beloved tale. <br /><br />Thank you Stephanie. Better late than never. <u>A Little Princess</u> was an enchanting read.<br /><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17081037593366091435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_78737746" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78737746" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78737746?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=school-story">school-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78737746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6102233625574377199">Now as much as Frances Hodgson Burnett's <u>A Little Princess</u> is and remains both a childhood and adulthood favourite, in some if not actually many ways, Sara Crewe and her entire demeanour do at times appear as being simply and frustratingly just a bit too good to be true. And while I have indeed always liked Sara's story tremendously, I also must admit that I have never loved it as much as, say, <u>The Secret Garden</u> (also, of course, by Frances Hodgson Burnett) or the Anne of Green Gables and the Em</span>
  <span id="freeText6102233625574377199" style="display:none">Now as much as Frances Hodgson Burnett's <u>A Little Princess</u> is and remains both a childhood and adulthood favourite, in some if not actually many ways, Sara Crewe and her entire demeanour do at times appear as being simply and frustratingly just a bit too good to be true. And while I have indeed always liked Sara's story tremendously, I also must admit that I have never loved it as much as, say, <u>The Secret Garden</u> (also, of course, by Frances Hodgson Burnett) or the Anne of Green Gables and the Emily of New Moon series (Lucy Maud Montgomery). For in all of these here novels, the main characters are presented as having their share of faults (and at times even seriously problematic and major ones), while in <u>A Little Princess</u>, Sara Crewe seemingly has little or no such peccadilloes (except perhaps that she does at times appear almost patronising in her goodness and her feelings for <i>the populace</i>, but I think that the author, that Frances Hodgson Burnett actually does not mean this to be considered as a fault, and it is just our more modern sensibilities which tend to make us consider this kind of <i>noblesse oblige</i> feeling to be not entirely, not altogether praiseworthy anymore). <br /><br />And actually, one important consideration to keep in mind is that <u>A Little Princess</u> was published quite a few years before <u>The Secret Garden</u> (the fomer was published in 1905, I believe, and I think <u>The Secret Garden</u> was not published until 1911 or so, and the novella on which <u>A Little Princess</u> is based, <u>Sara Crewe, Or What Happened At Miss Minchin's</u> was actually published even earlier, around 1888). And thus, perhaps Frances Hodgson Burnett's attitude towards children had matured by the time she penned <u>The Secret Garden</u>, and she might have by then realised that it would be better to have main characters who are not perfect, but also have their share of not so stellar character traits. But on the other hand, I also have to wonder whether the author might not have deliberately portrayed Sara as a faultless princess-like character because she wanted to portray her as some kind of magical, fairy tale like entity (a child-goddess of compassion, helpful, patient, accepting, but ultimately too good to be true, a bit like the type of character Dickon represents in <u>The Secret Garden</u>, similarly godlike and unrealistic, but then, Dickon is a supporting character and not the main character, like Sara is in <u>A Little Princess</u>). <br /><br />Still, <u>A Little Princess</u> truly is and always will be a lovely and sweet tale (somewhat of an upside down fairy tale, a riches to rags and then back to riches story) and a novel that although written more than a century ago, is still enjoyable, readable and for most children, approachable (and I bet for many adults are like me, having not just fond childhood memories of <u>A little Princess</u>, but also of repeated rereads).</span>
  <a data-text-id="6102233625574377199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_138851935" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138851935" />
    <a title="Zeek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2478293-zeek"><img alt="Zeek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339154824p2/2478293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138851935?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zeek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zeek" href="/user/show/2478293-zeek">Zeek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8135560-a-little-princess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=children-books">children-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=literary">literary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=favorites-all-time">favorites-all-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138851935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer423635793705540314">The story begins with little Sara Crewe traveling from the life she’s always known living in India with her beloved Father, Captain Crewe, to be schooled like all proper British girls in London. Her father is loathe to let her go but knows he must for her own good. Almost immediately upon arrival, Sara sees quite clearly with her wise beyond her years insight that Miss Minchin, the proprietor of the school, is not a fair lady, although she hides it well enough. Just as immediately, Sara gets the</span>
  <span id="freeText423635793705540314" style="display:none">The story begins with little Sara Crewe traveling from the life she’s always known living in India with her beloved Father, Captain Crewe, to be schooled like all proper British girls in London. Her father is loathe to let her go but knows he must for her own good. Almost immediately upon arrival, Sara sees quite clearly with her wise beyond her years insight that Miss Minchin, the proprietor of the school, is not a fair lady, although she hides it well enough. Just as immediately, Sara gets the reputation of being a little princess as her father lavishly buys cloths, dolls and comfortable living quarters. But Sara is not the spoiled child you might think her to be, no- quite the opposite. She could have cared less for all the finery if only to stay with her Papa, but of course society says otherwise and far too quickly she is left behind.<br /><br />Miss Minchin doesn’t make it easy for Sara, of course, but because she values Sara’s money, she plays along with Captain Crewe’s desires of spoiling the child- even when Sara unintentionally repeatedly reveals with her calm spirit that she is far more clever than the mean-spirited proprietress of the boarding school. Then, on the very day of Sara’s 11th birthday, news arrive that her father has passed away, and not only that- all of his money is lost as well.<br /><br />Miss Minchin, feeling as if tricked into covering Sara’s expenses- expenses assured to be covered by the wealthy Captain Crewe- Miss Minchin takes out her wrath on the grieving child and makes her the drudge of the school, a step only slighter higher than the scullery maid Becky, whom Sara has befriended. <br /><br />For years Sara suffers under the control of Minchin, doing all the tasks the servants don’t want to do, going to bed starving and cold each night. <br /><br />But, try as she might, Miss Minchin couldn’t bring the clever girl down to the lowered station she thought she deserved to be in. For Sara Crewe was an expert at bolstering herself with imaginations. <br /><br />When Minchin was at her worst, Sara’s proud spirit pretended she was soldier on a long and weary march. When given nothing but crumbs she shared it with her friend Mechezzidek, the rat who lived in the wall whom Sara pretended had a large family to take care of. No matter how hungry- she gave. She gave stories to a forlorn student whom the other students looked down upon for being fat and stupid and gave unheard of friendship to Becky, a mere scullery maid, who stayed in the room in the attic right next to her. She even gave away a boon she fell upon quite by accident one day while running errands- all because she believed a true Princess, like the one she imagined herself to be, is not one to complain or take things for herself when aid is needed for the populace.<br /><br />One day the school becomes abuzz with the news that a wealthy man is moving next door and Sara in her clever mind quickly assigns a story to him to entertain herself in the hours after her drudgery is over, to keep her mind off her hunger. Her curiosity is even more aroused when she meets the wealthy man’s native Indian man servant and his pet monkey one evening when the monkey escapes into her attic window. <br /><br />Ram Dass, the man servant, is struck by the bright child, and from that moment on, watches with silent eyes and ears every kind thing Sara does and eventually brings it to the wealthy man’s attention. Sensing they can help her, The wealthy neighbor and Ram Dass determine to bless the girl who gives so much yet is treated so poorly- Ram Dass because he knows exactly what’s going on, the wealthy man because the child reminds him of another young girl he lost and is desperate to find.<br /><br />One evening Sara, possibly at her coldest and hungriest, welcomes her friend Ermengarde into her room. Ermengarde finally realizing how the kindest person in her world is being treated, promptly decides to share a basket sent to her from home, stuffed with treats and food. Delighted Sara arranges the room as a secret surprise for Ermengarde and Becky, while Ermengarde leaves to retrieve the food. When the girls gather together, Sara transports the little group as if by magic to a grand ballroom prepared for a feast, all the while staying in their drab little room. It’s a wondrous time for all the girls, trying with all the might to imagine the beautiful room right along with Sara.<br /><br />Of course the evil Miss Minchin ruins it. <br /><br />But perhaps she wouldn’t have been so adamant in putting the little princess in her place if she knew that her actions would become the catalyst for Sara to be blessed beyond her own very vivid imagination.<br /><br />I would have loved this story as a kid, but I love it even more now. I’ve always loved a heroine I can root for and a villain I can despise- and this story delivers them! Sara is exactly the kind of girl I admired growing up and one I longed to be. Clever, pretty, just a bit odd but oh so noble. Yeah I never quite attained such nobility nor cleverness and prettiness, but I wanted to and that’s saying something I guess. :)<br /><br />I was totally engaged while listening to this story and I cant wait to share it with my nieces! I highly recommend it as an entertaining read but also as a good reminder for every child- if we imagine ourselves as noble princesses- even even though the world sees us as beggars- one day we may become one… in spirit if not in truth!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="423635793705540314" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
